plt.style.use('default') plt.rcParams['font.sans-serif'] = ['Arial'] plt.rcParams['axes.unicode_minus'] = False A = [1.7, 1.8, 1.64, 1.55, 1.32, 1.51, 1.64, 1.69, 1.77, 1.42] B = [2.56, 2.69, 2.65, 1.99, 2.13, 2.64, 2.35, 2.56, 2.55, 2.12] C = [2.12, 2.23, 2.64, 1.96, 1.89, 1.68, 2.21, 2.65, 2.66, 2.68] data = [A, B, C] x_labels = ['P', 'P', 'T'] colors = ['#000000', '#1BB6AFFF', '#D65B5AFF'] fig, ax1 = plt.subplots(figsize=(12, 8), dpi=100) for i, sample in enumerate(data): box = ax1.boxplot( [sample], patch_artist=True, positions=[i + 1], widths=0.5, boxprops=dict(facecolor=colors[i], color="black", linewidth=1.5, alpha=0.5), whiskerprops=dict(color="black", linewidth=1.5), capprops=dict(color="black", linewidth=1.5), medianprops=dict(color="red", linewidth=2), edgecolor="black", s=50) ax1.set_xticks(np.arange(len(x_labels)) + 1) ax1.set_xticklabels(x_labels, fontsize=28) ax1.set_ylabel("OCP (V)", fontsize=28, labelpad=20) ax1.set_ylim(1.0, 3.0) for i, sample in enumerate(data): mean = np.mean(sample) ax1.text(i + 1, mean + 0.05, f"{mean:.2f}", ha='center', fontsize=20, color="white") ax2 = ax1.twinx() scaled_data = [[x * 5 for x in sample] for sample in data] print(scaled_data) for i, sample in enumerate(scaled_data): kde = sns.kdeplot( y=sample, ax=ax2, bw_adjust=0.5, color=colors[i], linewidth=2.5, fill=True, alpha=0.5, label=x_labels[i] ) if kde.get_lines(): density_line = kde.get_lines()[-1] x, y = density_line.get_data() max_density = max(x) x_normalized = x/ max_density kde.get_lines()[-1].set_data(x_normalized, y) ax2.set_xlabel("Normalized Density", fontsize=28, labelpad=20) ax2.tick_params(axis='x', which='major', labelsize=20) ax2.set_xlim(0,4) ax2.get_yaxis().set_visible(False) ax1.tick_params(axis='both', A thought experiment is a hypothetical situation in which a hypothesis, theory,or principle is laid out for the purpose of thinking through its consequences. The concept is also referred to using the German-language term Gedankenexperiment within the work of the physicist Ernst Mach and includes thoughts about what may have occurred if a different course of action were taken. The importance of this ability is that it allows the experimenter to imagine what may occur in the future, as well as the implications of alternate courses of action. @Wikipedia æ€æƒ³å®éªŒï¼ˆThought running listening podcast Trevor Noah Write little and often. A good nap solves a lot of productivity problems. ï¼ˆ@lexfridman Jun 11ï¼‰ "I'll start tomorrow" â†©ï¸ The biggest lie you tell yourself is that you'll do something you should really be doing tomorrow or at some other time. This often leads to not doing it at all, resulting in a loss of trust in yourself. You keep putting something off until you reach a point where you completely abandon it because you lack confidence in yourself. If you truly intend to do something or really need to, do it now without hesitation and without excuses, because that's when you'll overcome yourself and it will be much easier for you in the future. You don't even have to do the whole thing; on the contrary, start small, because often the beginning is the hardest and requires the most effort. The more you overcome this initial hurdle, the easier it will be to continue. So, the next time you have something planned, whether it's chores like homework or cleaning, or things you've always wanted to do like a solo date or learning a new language, start NOW in small steps and don't put it off to the future, because then you'll NEVER do it. Tip â†©ï¸ The 5-Minute Rule If it takes less than 5 minutes, do it now. Yes, even if itâ€™s getting up to stretch. Procrastination is for stretching, not tasks! Eat the Frog First Tackle the hardest task first thing in the morning. Frogs taste better when youâ€™re not thinking about them all day. Pomodoro Technique Work for 25 minutes, then take a 5-minute break. Repeat. Because even tomatoes need a break! Make a To-Do List Write down your tasks. Checking them off feels like a tiny victory dance every time. Set Alarms Use alarms to remind you of tasks. Because nothing says "Get back to work" like a phone screaming at you. Delegate Share tasks with others. Remember, teamwork makes the dream work (and gives you more Netflix time). Avoid Multitasking Focus on one task at a time. Multitasking is just doing multiple things poorly at once. Use Apps and Tools Utilize productivity apps. Let technology be the boss that tells you to get back to work. Break Tasks into Chunks Divide tasks into smaller, manageable parts. Eating an elephant is easier one bite at a time, not that you should eat elephants. Set Boundaries Learn to say no. Protect your time like itâ€™s the last slice of pizza. Reward Yourself Give yourself a treat after completing tasks. Because who doesnâ€™t work faster for chocolate? Keep a Calendar Schedule your tasks and appointments. Because remembering everything is for elephants and computers, not humans. Take Care of Yourself Get enough sleep, exercise, and eat well. A tired brain is like a computer running Windows 95. Slow and prone to crash. Limit Social Media Use social media blockers during work hours. Facebook and Instagram can wait; your research paper canâ€™t. Reflect and Adjust Review your progress regularly and adjust as needed. Itâ€™s like GPS rerouting you after a wrong turn. å²ä¸Šå«é‡‘é‡æœ€é«˜çš„cheatsheet â†©ï¸ Top 4 Productivity Methods pic.twitter.com/WsF4t0T2il— Atomic Habits | James Clear (@1AtomicHabits) June 16, 2024 Thanks for being an insider till the end! ç°ä»£ç”µæ¢¯ä½¿ç”¨æ›´å¤æ‚çš„å¯å‘å¼ç®—æ³•æ¥å†³å®šä¸‹ä¸€ä¸ªæœåŠ¡è¯·æ±‚ã€‚ç”µæ¢¯ç›®çš„åœ°è°ƒåº¦å°±æ˜¯ä¸€ä¸ªå¾ˆå¥½çš„ä¾‹å­ã€‚å®ƒä½¿ç”¨ä¸€ç§ç®—æ³•æ¥å†³å®šå°†å“ªè¾†è½¿å¢åˆ†é…åˆ°å“ªé‡Œä»¥åŠæœ€ä½³æœåŠ¡æ—¶é—´ã€‚ å›åˆ°ç”µæ¢¯æ§åˆ¶çš„èƒŒåç®—æ³•ï¼ˆå«æœ‰Javascriptä»£ç å®ç°)ï¼š How does an elevator works? Hoes does an elevator work? Every elevator works differently based on its real-world allocation and it's fairly difficult to build such an algorithm. All algorithms might differ from each other but looking at the most basic example, an elevator is using the so-called C-SCAN algorithm. This algorithm is used for Disk Scheduling also known as I/O scheduling. From an elevator perspective, the algorithm works as follows: Request array represents an array storing which floors the elevator has been requested from The elevator services always from floor 0 to the highest floor. While moving down, the elevator does not service any of the requests. When the elevator reaches the beginning (floor 0), reverse the direction. While moving up, the elevator services all floors one by one. Currently serviced floor now becomes the new position of the elevator. Go to step 6 until the elevator reaches the highest floor. If the elevator reaches the highest floor, reverse the direction and go to step 3 until all requests have been serviced. Going through the steps you can see that there are some performance optimisations which can be done here. For example: Point 3, the elevator will be quicker if it services any outstanding requests going down to floor 0. Point 7 - there is no point of going to the highest floor if there isn't a request for that floor Point 8 - it will make more sense to reverse the direction once the highest request has been serviced "Philly shell" is a defensive boxing stance or strategy that is associated with fighters from Philadelphia, hence the name. This defensive technique involves holding the lead hand low and close to the body, positioning the shoulder to protect the chin, and using head movement to slip and dodge punches. The rear hand is typically held higher to provide additional protection. Fighters utilizing the Philly shell rely on quick reflexes, upper body movement, and counter-punching to evade attacks while creating opportunities to launch their own offensive moves. It's a distinctive and often effective defensive style that has been employed by various successful boxers, contributing to its recognition in the world of combat sports. Mainly these days, people wonder whether it's necessary to learn languages "in person"? As a matter of fact, we've already used AI models to generate code for so many times, so is it vital that I could handle the code without AI? "One thing I am reasonably confident predicting, however, is that LLMs wonâ€™t make learning obsolete, " Scott Young wrote in the newsletter. He took paper writing and a calculator as examples. The saying goes, 'The palest ink is better than the best memory.' We no longer need to memorize speeches if the full text is written down. To some extent, our memory of the mind gets released. While they certainly eliminate the need to learn some skills (I have no idea how to use a slide rule, for instance), we still have to understand arithmetic to use a calculator to get the answer we seek, even if the machine does the actual computation. Knowledge outside your head doesnâ€™t count, since it canâ€™t participate in learning and reasoning. The ability to look something up is not a substitute for having knowledge in your head. Understanding an LLMâ€™s answer depends heavily on the knowledge you already possess. Your own knowledge allows you to extract knowledge from the LLM more accurately. LLMs may accelerate the need for knowledge, since the combination of [knowledgeable person + ChatGPT] will outperform [ignorant person + ChatGPT] by a wider margin than exists between the two people on their own. From what I can see, like generating codes by ChatGPT, it'd be better if the users are capable of reading, finding out the errors and correcting the codes. Wait but somehow all these products which are tokens as examples are not as epoch-making as LLMs. So we can barely see it that way. Or maybe LLMs are not that epoch-making yet, we all can just see it as a new-era tool. The larger and stronger-impact AI products are in the way... Physical labour can be replaced by AI techs definitely. But even sophisticated enough tasks like chess have already been proven that can defeat in front of AI. In the extreme case, all bets are off. Perhaps weâ€™ll live in a utopian future where machines do all the work and people do cognitive activities for leisure or showing off, much like gardening is a hobby, not agriculture.
